TITLE: Boat Rental Marbella 2026: Yachts, Catamarans &amp; Charters
DESCRIPTION: Boat rental in Marbella from €749 for 2h on our 12.5 m flybridge motor yachts (Astondoa 40 + Azimut 39). Departing Puerto Banús. Skipper, fuel, drinks, insurance and VAT included.

We operate a 27-boat fleet in Marbella, led by two 12.5 m flybridge motor yachts — the Astondoa 40 and the Azimut 39 — all departing Puerto Banús with licensed skipper, fuel, drinks, insurance and VAT included. Prices start at €749 for 2 hours and run up to €2,299 for a full 8-hour day . This page is the full overview — fleet, ports, license rules and how to book. Skip the long-form below and message us on WhatsApp for an instant quote with real-time availability across all five ports. Boat rental Marbella prices in 2026 Same boat, same crew, transparent hourly pricing. No high-season uplift, no levante surcharge, no marina fee added at the dock. Duration Price What you get 2 hours €749 Quick spin along the Golden Mile, one swim stop 4 hours €1,299 Half-day — comfortable lunch + swim 6 hours €1,799 Two swim stops, paddleboard, real day out 8 hours €2,299 Full day — Sotogrande or Cabopino itineraries Full grid and per-boat detail at /boats/ . Compare the Astondoa 40 (9 guests, Spanish-built, classic Mediterranean styling) vs the Azimut 39 (11 guests, Italian flybridge, modern lines). Astondoa or Azimut? Both boats are the same length (12.5 m), price (€749 → €2,299), and depart from the same marina (Puerto Banús). What differs: Astondoa 40 — Spanish-built, classic teak and cream interior, up to 9 guests . The "Fufi" you see in our photos. Best for couples and groups up to 8 who want the local Mediterranean feel. Azimut 39 — Italian-built flybridge, modern lines, up to 11 guests . Pick this one for larger groups (9+) or anyone who wants the upper sun-deck experience. Departure ports: Puerto Banús, Marbella Marina, Cabopino, Estepona, Sotogrande Puerto Banús is the default departure for any boat over 12 metres and for everything that calls itself a luxury yacht. It sits 7 km west of Marbella old town, has the deepest berths, and puts the lined-up Ferraris on display as you walk to the pontoon. Marbella Marina (officially Puerto Deportivo Virgen del Carmen) is far more central, walking distance from any old-town hotel, and ideal for guests with mobility constraints. Cabopino, 12 km east, is the quietest pickup point and the closest to the dune beaches; licence-free rentals are concentrated here. Estepona and Sotogrande add another 30 minutes by car each way and are usually only worth it if you're staying there. Our full Puerto Banús vs Marbella Marina comparison covers parking, walking distance and which boats live where. Licence rules you actually need to know You do not need a Spanish boat licence to rent in Marbella as long as either (a) the boat is small enough to fall under the licence-free rules, or (b) the charter comes with a qualified skipper — the case for ~95% of bookings on this site. The licence-free thresholds in Spain are: hull up to 5 metres, motor up to 15 hp, sail up to 6 metres, distance from coast up to 2 nautical miles, daylight hours only, captain at least 18 years old. A quick test before you self-drive: are you confident reversing into a windy berth at Cabopino with a queue of boats waiting? If not, book with a skipper. Full rule details: see our Spain boat licence rules 2026 guide, including what changes if you hold a UK ICC or RYA Day Skipper certificate (you can charter larger boats without a Spanish licence — bring the original certificate, not a copy). What's included — and what is not Standard inclusions on a Marbella skippered charter are the captain, fuel for a normal coastal cruising itinerary, soft drinks and water, ice, light snacks, towels, snorkelling masks and an inflatable donut or paddleboard. What's not included by default: alcohol on board (you can BYO on most boats, ask first), prepared lunch (€25–€60 per head depending on caterer), berth taxes for stops in non-home ports, and tip for the skipper (€20–€50 is normal for a good day, or 10% on luxury charters). Typical itineraries from Marbella Half-day from Puerto Banús: head west past Estepona, stop for a swim at Cala del Faro, optional tapas at Sotogrande, back by sunset. Full-day from Marbella Marina: east towards Cabopino's dunes and snorkel anchorage at Cala Cortés, lunch on board, then ice cream stop in the Cabopino port itself. Two-hour sunset: cruise the Golden Mile coastline at displacement speed, anchor briefly off Nikki Beach, return as the sun drops behind La Concha. A Gibraltar day trip (see our Gibraltar by boat piece) is doable from Sotogrande but adds 80 NM round trip and only makes sense in flat sea. How to book in 60 seconds Three ways: WhatsApp us with your date, group size and rough budget — instant quotes from local operators, no account, no deposit until you confirm. Call if you want to talk through itinerary options first. Browse our 27-boat fleet at /boats/ if you'd rather pick a specific hull yourself. Whichever route you pick, the price you see is what you pay — no booking fees added at checkout, no surprise marina charges. Same advice applies whether you're after a luxury yacht rental Marbella for a corporate day out or a quick 2-hour spin from the central Puerto Banús pontoon. Your browser doesn't support HTML5 video. Follow @boatrentalmarbella Frequently asked questions How much does it cost to rent a boat in Marbella? Boat rental in Marbella on our fleet starts at €749 for 2 hours and runs to €2,299 for a full 8-hour day. Same price across seasons. Every charter includes licensed skipper, fuel, drinks, insurance and Spanish IVA (VAT). For larger groups (9+ guests on Azimut 39) the per-person cost drops to about €70 for the 2-hour cruise. Where do boats depart from in Marbella? The five working pickup points are Puerto Banús (the marquee yacht marina, west of Marbella town), Marbella Marina/Puerto Deportivo Virgen del Carmen (right by the central promenade), Cabopino (eastern Marbella, near the dunes), Estepona, and Sotogrande further west. Puerto Banús handles the largest yachts and most luxury bookings. Do I need a licence to rent a boat in Marbella? No. Spain allows licence-free rentals for boats up to 5 m hull length with engines up to 15 hp (or sail up to 6 m), within 2 nautical miles of the coast, in daylight, captain aged 18 or over. For anything larger, you either hold a PNB/PER licence or — by far the most common option — book a charter with the skipper included. What is included in the price? Every charter on our Astondoa 40 or Azimut 39 includes: licensed Spanish skipper, fuel for the standard coastal route, soft drinks and water, snorkel gear, inflatable donut, paddleboard, towels, insurance and Spanish IVA (VAT). Catered lunch (€25–€60 per head) is the main optional add-on. When is the best time to rent a boat in Marbella? June and September are the sweet spot — warm sea (22–24 °C), long sunshine hours, fewer afternoon levante winds than July–August, and prices roughly 10–15% under peak. July and August are busiest and warmest but choppier from 14:00 onwards. April–May and October still deliver flat morning seas at noticeably lower rates. How far in advance should I book? For July, August and any Saturday in summer, book 2–4 weeks ahead — the larger yachts (15 m+) sell out first. For weekday trips in May, June, September or October, 3–5 days is usually enough. For licence-free boats and weekday 2-hour sunset cruises, same-day WhatsApp bookings are routinely possible. Can children come on the boat? Yes — virtually every operator welcomes children. TITLE: Astondoa 40 vs Pershing 46: Which Yacht Suits Your Marbella Charter?
DESCRIPTION: Compare Astondoa 40 vs Pershing 46 for your Marbella charter. See specs, capacity, pricing, and which suits your group. Book now.

Home › Astondoa 40 vs Pershing 46: Which Yacht Suits Your Marbella Charter? Choosing between the Astondoa 40 and Pershing 46 for your Marbella charter? Both depart from Puerto Banús and offer premium experiences, but they suit different budgets and group sizes. This comparison breaks down the key differences in size, capacity, pricing, and inclusions to help you decide which yacht fits your day on the Costa del Sol. Size and Capacity The Astondoa 40 measures 12.5 metres and accommodates up to 9 passengers. The Pershing 46 is larger at 14 metres, with a maximum capacity of 10 guests. For groups of 10, the Pershing is the only option; for 9 or fewer, the Astondoa offers ample space. Both yachts provide sunbathing areas, a saloon, and a small galley, but the Pershing's extra length gives slightly more deck room. Pricing and Value The Astondoa 40 has transparent pricing: €749 for 2 hours, scaling up to €2,299 for 8 hours. This includes a skipper, fuel, drinks (water, soft drinks, beer, white wine, cava), light snacks, insurance, and Spanish IVA. The Pershing 46 is priced on request via WhatsApp, making it less straightforward for budget planning but potentially negotiable for longer charters. For cost certainty, the Astondoa 40 wins. Inclusions and Amenities Both charters include the same standard package: licensed skipper, fuel, water, soft drinks, beer, white wine, cava, light snacks, insurance, safety equipment, and 21% IVA. No hidden extras. The Pershing 46 may offer more premium finishes, but the core inclusions are identical. You can bring your own food on either yacht, and catering is available on request. Performance and Style The Pershing 46 is known for sporty lines and higher performance, appealing to those who want a faster, more dynamic ride. The Astondoa 40 is a classic flybridge cruiser, prioritising comfort and stability at cruising speeds. Both are well-maintained and depart from Puerto Banús, giving you direct access to Marbella Bay, Cabopino, and Estepona. Ideal Use Cases Choose the Astondoa 40 if: you have 9 or fewer guests, want fixed pricing from €749, and prefer a simple, all-inclusive booking. Perfect for a half-day trip to Cala del Faro or a sunset cruise along the Golden Mile. Choose the Pershing 46 if: your group is 10 people, you value a sportier design, and you're flexible on budget. Ideal for full-day excursions to Sotogrande or longer coastal tours. Which Departs from Puerto Banús? Both yachts operate from Puerto Banús, the iconic marina in Marbella. This means easy access to restaurants, shops, and parking. Whether you choose the Astondoa 40 or Pershing 46, you'll start your charter from the heart of the Costa del Sol's luxury scene. Explore our full fleet for more options. Frequently asked questions Which is bigger, Astondoa 40 or Pershing 46? The Pershing 46 is larger at 14 metres (46 ft) compared to the Astondoa 40 at 12.5 metres (40 ft). The Pershing offers more deck space and a higher passenger capacity (10 vs 9). Can I book the Pershing 46 for a 2-hour trip? Pricing for the Pershing 46 is on request, so you can ask for shorter durations. However, the Astondoa 40 has a fixed rate of €749 for 2 hours, making it a more straightforward option for quick trips. What's included in the Astondoa 40 charter price? The Astondoa 40 rate includes a licensed skipper, fuel, water, soft drinks, beer, white wine, cava, light snacks, insurance, safety equipment, and Spanish IVA (21%). No hidden costs. Which yacht is better for a group of 10? The Pershing 46 can take up to 10 passengers, while the Astondoa 40 is capped at 9. For a full group of 10, choose the Pershing 46. For 9 or fewer, the Astondoa 40 works well. Do both yachts depart from the same marina? Yes, both the Astondoa 40 and Pershing 46 depart from Puerto Banús in Marbella. This makes them equally convenient for exploring the Costa del Sol coastline. Is the Pershing 46 faster than the Astondoa 40? Both are motor yachts, but exact speeds are not specified. The Pershing 46 is a performance-oriented model known for speed, while the Astondoa 40 offers a comfortable cruise. Contact us for specific performance details. Can I bring my own food on either yacht? Yes, you are welcome to bring your own food. Each charter includes complimentary drinks and light snacks. Catering can also be arranged on request for both yachts. How do I book the Pershing 46? To book the Pershing 46, contact us via WhatsApp for pricing and availability. The Astondoa 40 can be booked directly online with fixed rates starting at €749 for 2 hours. ★★★★★ 4.9 · verified reviews From €749 2h skippered charter Instant quotes from local operators across Puerto Banús, Marbella Marina, Cabopino, Estepona & Sotogrande. 💬 Message on WhatsApp Avg reply < 5 min · No deposit until you confirm 📅 Book now Browse the full fleet → All charters include Licensed skipper & fuel Drinks: water, soft drinks, beer, white wine, cava Light snacks Insurance & safety equipment Snorkel gear & inflatables VAT 21% — no surprises

TITLE: Azimut 58 vs Sunseeker Predator 74: Marbella Yacht Showdown
DESCRIPTION: Azimut 58 vs Sunseeker Predator 74 Marbella: compare size, speed, price &amp; luxury. Which yacht suits your charter? Book your day from Puerto Banús.

Home › Azimut 58 vs Sunseeker Predator 74: Marbella Yacht Showdown Choosing between the Azimut 58 Flybridge and the Sunseeker Predator 74 for your Marbella yacht charter? Both are luxury powerboats, but they cater to different tastes. The Azimut 58 (17.6m, 12 pax) is a flybridge cruiser perfect for lounging and socialising, while the Predator 74 (22.5m, 12 pax) is a sportier open yacht built for speed. This guide breaks down the differences in size, speed, price, and local cruising experience to help you decide. We operate the Azimut 58 from Puerto Banús—the Predator 74 is available via other operators but we’ll compare them fairly. For the full range of boats available, browse our boat rental Marbella hub. Size and Layout The Azimut 58 Flybridge measures 17.6 metres and features a spacious flybridge with a sunpad, dining area, and steering station. Below deck, you’ll find three cabins and two heads. The Predator 74 is larger at 22.5 metres, with a more open-plan layout—no flybridge, but a vast cockpit and foredeck sunbathing area. The Predator’s extra length gives more interior volume, often with four cabins. For groups prioritising al fresco lounging, the Azimut 58’s flybridge is a clear advantage. Performance and Speed The Sunseeker Predator 74 is built for thrill-seekers, with twin MAN engines pushing it to 38–40 knots. The Azimut 58 Flybridge cruises at 22–26 knots, which is ample for reaching Cala del Faro or Estepona in 30–40 minutes. If you want to feel the wind in your hair and cover more coastline quickly, the Predator wins. For a relaxed cruise with drinks and conversation, the Azimut is the better choice. Pricing Comparison Our Azimut 58 Flybridge pricing is on request via WhatsApp, but expect €2,500–€4,000 for a half-day (4–5 hours) and up to €6,000 for a full day, all inclusive. The Sunseeker Predator 74 typically starts at €5,000 for a half-day and can exceed €8,000 for a full day, due to its larger size and higher fuel consumption. Both include a skipper, fuel, drinks, and snacks. For budget-conscious groups, the Azimut 58 offers excellent value without sacrificing luxury. Local Cruising: Marbella to Sotogrande Departing Puerto Banús , both yachts can explore the same iconic stops: Marbella Marina , Cabopino , Cala Cortés , and Sotogrande . The Azimut 58’s flybridge is perfect for spotting La Concha mountain while anchored. The Predator’s open bow allows for sunbathing at Río Verde . For a longer cruise to Estepona (about 10 NM), the Predator gets you there faster, but the Azimut offers a more leisurely journey with better social spaces. Which Yacht Should You Choose? Choose the Azimut 58 Flybridge if you value comfort, social lounging, and a flybridge view. It’s ideal for families or groups wanting a relaxed day with dining, swimming, and sunbathing. Choose the Sunseeker Predator 74 if you want a sportier, faster experience and don’t mind a more open layout. If you’re set on the Azimut 58, book the Azimut 58 Flybridge directly from our fleet. For other options, see our full fleet . Frequently asked questions Which is faster, Azimut 58 or Sunseeker Predator 74? The Sunseeker Predator 74 typically reaches 38–40 knots, while the Azimut 58 Flybridge cruises at 22–26 knots. The Predator is built for speed; the Azimut for cruising comfort. Can I charter a Sunseeker Predator 74 in Marbella? Yes, through other operators. Our fleet does not include a Predator 74, but we offer the Azimut 58 Flybridge, which provides a similar luxury experience from Puerto Banús. How many people can the Azimut 58 carry? The Azimut 58 Flybridge accommodates up to 12 passengers, making it ideal for groups of friends or family. The Sunseeker Predator 74 also holds 12 pax. What is the price difference between Azimut 58 and Predator 74? Our Azimut 58 pricing is on request via WhatsApp, typically €2,500–€4,000 for a half-day. The Predator 74 generally costs €5,000–€8,000+ per day, reflecting its larger size and higher speed. Which yacht is better for a relaxing day in Marbella? The Azimut 58 Flybridge, with its spacious deck and flybridge lounging, is perfect for relaxing. The Predator 74 is better for those wanting a sportier ride and faster coastal hops. Where do charters depart from? Both the Azimut 58 (our boat) and most Predator 74 charters in Marbella depart from Puerto Banús, the main luxury marina on the Costa del Sol. What is included with the Azimut 58 charter? Every charter includes a licensed skipper, fuel, water, soft drinks, beer, white wine, cava, light snacks, insurance, safety equipment, and Spanish IVA (21%). Can I anchor for swimming on either yacht? Yes, both yachts can anchor at spots like Cala del Faro, Cala Cortés, or off Cabopino. The Azimut 58’s flybridge offers great views while swimming. ★★★★★ 4.9 · verified reviews From €749 2h skippered charter Instant quotes from local operators across Puerto Banús, Marbella Marina, Cabopino, Estepona & Sotogrande. 💬 Message on WhatsApp Avg reply < 5 min · No deposit until you confirm 📅 Book now Browse the full fleet → All charters include Licensed skipper & fuel Drinks: water, soft drinks, beer, white wine, cava Light snacks Insurance & safety equipment Snorkel gear & inflatables VAT 21% — no surprises

What you can and can't do Yes: BYO alcohol on private charters, loud music at anchor outside marina limits, jumping off the boat at the anchor stop, costume changes on board, inflatable swans, drone photography (your own pilot). No: glass on deck (cans and plastic only on most boats), confetti or anything that ends up in the water (Spanish marina fines are punishing), open flames (no shisha or candles), drugs (the skipper will return to port and the deposit is forfeit). Spanish maritime alcohol law applies to the skipper, not guests — but be sensible. Best months for a Marbella boat party Late June through early September is peak — water at 22–24 °C, long daylight, the marina scene at full volume. July is the busiest single month. Mid-September keeps the warmth and drops the price 10–15%. May, June and October work for groups happy with 19–21 °C water (swims are shorter but everything else still flies). Outside that window party charters still run but the on-deck temperature won't sustain a long anchor stop. TITLE: Boat Rental Marbella No License 2026: Self-Drive 5m / 15hp Boats
DESCRIPTION: License-free boat rules in Spain (5m / 15hp / 2 NM). Our skippered fleet starts at €749 — no license needed because we provide the captain. Full guide to no-license boating in Marbella.

Home › Boat Rental Marbella No License 2026: Self-Drive 5m / 15hp Boats Skip the licence question: our fleet ( Astondoa 40 , Azimut 39 ) is crewed by a licensed skipper, so you don't need any license at all. From €749 for 2 h , group capacity 9–11 guests. The page below covers the licence-free rules if you want to drive a smaller boat yourself. The short version: yes, you can rent a boat in Marbella with no licence, no certificate, and no formal sailing experience — as long as you stick to the Spanish rule set of 5 metres hull, 15 horsepower engine, 2 nautical miles from the coast, daylight only, and you're at least 18 years old. From €130 for 2 hours, this is the cheapest and most flexible way to get on the water on the Costa del Sol. The Spanish no-licence rules (2026) Spain's leisure boating regulation 875/2014 defines the licence-free category — known officially as navegación sin titulación — with the following limits: Hull length: 5 metres maximum for motor boats, 6 metres for sail-only boats. Engine power: 15 hp maximum (no exceptions — operators are checked). Distance from coast: 2 nautical miles (~3.7 km). Most coastal anchorages from Marbella sit well inside this. Time of day: daylight only. You must return before sunset. Captain age: 18 years or over with a valid ID. Alcohol: the same blood-alcohol limit as driving applies to the helm operator. For the broader licensing picture (and what you can charter if you have a foreign certificate), see our Spain boat licence rules guide. Where to pick up your no-licence boat Three Marbella locations operate licence-free fleets: Cabopino — biggest no-licence fleet on this stretch of coast. Easiest exit (the harbour mouth is wide and the immediate water is shallow and forgiving). Most affordable. Puerto Banús — fewer no-licence operators, slightly higher prices, but a great location if you want to anchor off Nikki Beach for the afternoon. Marbella Marina (Puerto Deportivo) — small no-licence fleet, central location, easy parking nearby. If you're staying further west, Estepona has additional licence-free operators that are 15–20% cheaper than Puerto Banús for the same boat. Skip the licence — book skippered If you want the simpler path: book our crewed fleet. Astondoa 40 and Azimut 39 run €749 for 2 h with the skipper included — no licence, no exam, no on-the-dock briefing. The page below explains the official Spanish licence-free rules for context, but they only apply if you want to drive a small (under 5 m / 15 hp) self-drive boat yourself. What to expect — your first time at the helm Arrive 30 minutes before departure. You'll show ID and credit card, sign a one-page rental contract, and the operator walks you through: Throttle and gear shift. One lever — forward, neutral, reverse. Outboards on 15 hp boats are simple. Steering. Either a wheel or, on the smallest boats, a tiller. Anchor. How to drop it and how to retrieve it without trapping fingers. VHF radio. Channel 16 is emergency; you'll rarely need it within 2 NM. Coastal exclusion zones. The 200 m swimmer buoy zone along every Marbella beach — you cannot cross it under power. Refuel procedure. Where the fuel dock is, payment method. The whole briefing takes 10–15 minutes. Then you take the boat for a controlled lap of the marina with the operator watching from the dock, and after that you're on your own. Good itineraries for a 4-hour licence-free trip From Cabopino: head west 20 minutes to anchor off the Cabopino dune beach, swim and snorkel for an hour, push west another 15 minutes to Río Real, swim again, return to Cabopino with 30 minutes of buffer. Stays inside 2 NM the whole time. From Puerto Banús: head east 25 minutes to anchor off Nikki Beach (water is deeper here, anchor sets cleanly), swim, optional tender visit, return via the Golden Mile coastline so you see the famous waterfront mansions. Easy first-timer route. Is a no-licence boat right for you? Yes if: you're a group of 2–4, you want flexibility on timing, you'd rather drive yourself than be a passenger, and you're comfortable with light wind chop. No if: you're 6+ people (capacity is 4–5 max), you want speed (15 hp is slow), you want range (2 NM is tight), or you don't enjoy thinking about wind and tide. For larger groups, look at yacht charter Marbella with a skipper, or compare all options on the boat rental Marbella hub. Frequently asked questions Can I really rent a boat in Marbella without a licence? Yes. Spanish maritime law permits any adult over 18 to operate a boat up to 5 metres long with an engine up to 15 hp (or a sailboat up to 6 m), within 2 nautical miles of the coast, in daylight, with no licence and no formal training. You'll do a 10-minute on-the-dock briefing with the operator covering throttle, anchor and VHF radio, then you're on your way. What can a 15 hp boat actually do? A 5 m / 15 hp boat in Marbella cruises at 8–12 knots fully loaded with 4 adults, planes lightly when solo or with two. You'll comfortably reach the anchor spots off Marbella Marina, Río Verde or the Cabopino dunes within 20–30 minutes. Estepona and Puerto Banús-to-Cabopino in a day is realistic. How much is a no-license boat rental in Marbella? €130 for 2 hours in low season (October to May), €180 in high season (June to September). Full half-day (4 hours) is €220–€280. Full day (8 hours) is €380–€450. Most operators take a refundable security deposit of €200–€300. Is fuel included? Practice varies. About half of Marbella operators include fuel in the rental price; the other half operate on 'return with the tank as you found it'. Either way, a 15 hp engine burns very little — a 2-hour cruise typically uses €8–€15 of petrol. What happens if I damage the boat? Standard policy: the security deposit covers minor damage. For anything larger, every license-free rental in Spain comes with mandatory third-party liability insurance, which the operator carries. You're not personally liable beyond the deposit unless you've been reckless or drunk at the helm. ★★★★★ 4.9 · verified reviews From €749 2h skippered charter Instant quotes from local operators across Puerto Banús, Marbella Marina, Cabopino, Estepona & Sotogrande. 💬 Message on WhatsApp Avg reply < 5 min · No deposit until you confirm 📅 Book now Browse the full fleet → All charters include Licensed skipper & fuel Drinks: water, soft drinks, beer, white wine, cava Light snacks Insurance & safety equipment Snorkel gear & inflatables VAT 21% — no surprises

Why Puerto Banús dominates Marbella boat rental Three reasons it's the default departure port: Depth and berth size. Where to meet the boat Puerto Banús is laid out as eight long parallel pontoons running south-east into the harbour, numbered 1 through 8 from west to east: Pier Typical fleet Walk from car park 1 Superyachts 30 m+, charter brokers 3 min 2–3 Luxury motor yachts 14–22 m 5 min 4–5 Motor yachts 10–14 m, catamarans 6 min 6 Sportfishers, sailing yachts 7 min 7 Day boats, licence-free, small sailboats 8 min 8 Working fleet, fuel dock 10 min Your charter will send you the exact pier and slip number 24 hours before. TITLE: Cancellation Policy — Boat Rental Marbella
DESCRIPTION: Cancellation policy for Boat Rental Marbella charters: 100% refund 7+ days before, weather cancellations always refundable, transparent sliding scale.

Home › Cancellation Policy Effective 1 May 2026 · Apply to all skippered charters from Puerto Banús, Marbella Marina, Cabopino, Estepona and Sotogrande. Summary in one line Cancel 7+ days before = full refund. Skipper-cancelled for weather = full refund, always. Full schedule When you cancel Refund Notes 7+ days before charter 100% Full refund, no questions. 3–6 days before 50% The other 50% covers skipper hold + fuel sourcing. 48 hours – 3 days 25% Higher because we've usually turned other bookings down. Inside 48 hours 0% Booked period is committed. Day-of no-show 0% Skipper waited at the dock. Weather cancellations If the skipper cancels the charter because of wind, sea state or thunderstorm risk, you always get a 100% refund or a free reschedule to a date of your choice. The call is made the evening before based on Windguru / AEMET forecasts. Light rain alone is not a cancellation reason on the Costa del Sol — drizzle clears within minutes, the sea is usually flat. How to cancel Message Andra on WhatsApp with your booking date. Refunds are processed back to the original payment method within 3–7 business days. Rescheduling vs cancelling Rescheduling is always free if we can find a new date in the same season. If the new date is in a different season (e.g. December → August), the new-season price applies — we'll show you the difference before you confirm. Add-ons and catering Add-ons booked separately (catered lunch, photographer, custom decoration) follow the catering provider's own cancellation terms — we forward 100% of what we collect, no markup. We'll always show you those terms when you add the line item. Force majeure If the charter is impossible because of events outside our control (port closure, government health order, harbour-wide emergency), you get a 100% refund regardless of how close to the date. Travel insurance We recommend buying travel insurance with cruise / charter cover for any booking over €1,500. Standard travel insurance often excludes private yacht charter — read your policy. TITLE: Catamaran Rental Marbella for Families: Spacious and Stable
DESCRIPTION: Book a catamaran rental Marbella family charter for a spacious, stable day on the Costa del Sol. From €749/2h with skipper, drinks &amp; snacks included.

Home › Catamaran Rental Marbella for Families: Spacious and Stable If you are looking for a catamaran rental Marbella family charter that combines space, stability, and all-inclusive ease, the Lagoon 380 is your best option. Unlike monohull motor yachts, catamarans offer a wide, stable platform that does not roll in a swell, making them ideal for young children, elderly parents, or anyone prone to seasickness. Our Lagoon 380 departs from Puerto Banús and can carry up to 10 passengers plus a licensed skipper. Prices start at €749 for two hours and go up to €2,299 for a full eight-hour day – and that includes drinks, snacks, fuel, insurance, and tax. No hidden extras, no surprises. Why a catamaran works for families A catamaran’s twin-hull design gives it a much wider beam than a monohull of the same length. The Lagoon 380 measures 11.6 metres overall but offers a living space that feels more like a 15-metre yacht. The saloon opens directly onto the aft deck, creating a single indoor-outdoor area where parents can keep an eye on children while preparing snacks. Because the hulls are separate, there is no deep V-shaped cabin to trip over – the saloon floor is flat, and the side decks have high guardrails. Children can move around without the constant tilt of a heeling monohull. Our family-friendly catamaran: Lagoon 380 The Lagoon 380 is the only catamaran in our fleet. It is 11.6 metres long, 6.5 metres wide, and can take up to 10 passengers. It departs from Puerto Banús, Marbella’s most famous marina. The boat has four double cabins and two heads (toilets), so a large family can spread out. The forward trampoline nets are a favourite spot for children to lie on and watch the coastline. The shallow draft of just 1.2 metres means the skipper can anchor very close to the beach at spots like Cala del Faro or Cala Cortés, where the water is shallow and calm enough for safe swimming. What’s included in the price Every charter on our Lagoon 380 includes a licensed skipper, all fuel, insurance, Spanish IVA (21%), and a complimentary bar with soft drinks, beer, white wine, and cava. Light snacks are also provided. You do not need to bring anything except sunscreen and towels. The skipper handles navigation, anchoring, and safety briefings, so you can relax. If you want to bring your own food or a birthday cake, the galley has a fridge and a stove. There is no extra charge for mooring at a restaurant dock, though any restaurant bill is yours. Where you can go on a family catamaran trip Departing from Puerto Banús, you have several family-friendly routes. A popular half-day option heads east towards Cabopino, a protected dune reserve with a sandy beach and calm water. The distance is about 5 nautical miles, so the sailing time is short. For a full day, you can go west to Estepona or even Sotogrande, where the coastline opens up with wider bays. The skipper will anchor for swimming and snorkelling at spots like Cala Cortés, a small cove with clear water and rocky seabed. The shallow draft of the catamaran allows it to get closer to the shore than most motor yachts. Pricing and booking Our Lagoon 380 is priced in Tier A: €749 for two hours, €1,199 for four hours, €1,699 for six hours, and €2,299 for eight hours. All prices include skipper, fuel, drinks, snacks, insurance, and tax. For longer charters or custom requests, simply contact us via WhatsApp. We do not charge extra for cleaning or mooring. To see the full range of boats, visit our Marbella boat rental hub. Safety and comfort for all ages The Lagoon 380 has high bulwarks and guardrails all around, reducing the risk of falls. The saloon door can be latched open or closed, and the galley is equipped with a gas cooker and a fridge. Lifejackets for children and adults are on board, and the skipper will give a short safety briefing before departure. The boat’s stability means that even on a breezy day, you will not feel the constant rolling that can upset younger children. Many families choose a four-hour morning charter (10:00–14:00) when the sea is calmest and the sun is not too strong. Frequently asked questions Is the Lagoon 380 suitable for young children? Yes. The Lagoon 380’s wide beam and low freeboard make it very stable, so toddlers and older kids can move around safely. The skipper will anchor in calm, shallow bays like Cala Cortés where children can swim under supervision. What is included in the catamaran rental price? Every charter includes a licensed skipper, fuel, insurance, Spanish IVA (21%), and an open bar of soft drinks, beer, white wine, cava, plus light snacks. No extra charges for mooring or cleaning. How many people can the Lagoon 380 carry? The Lagoon 380 has a maximum capacity of 10 passengers plus the skipper. This makes it ideal for a family group or two families sharing the day. Do we need to bring our own food and drinks? No. Soft drinks, beer, white wine, cava, and light snacks are provided. If you want a specific meal or cake for a celebration, you can bring your own – there is a fridge and galley on board. Can we swim and snorkel during the trip? Absolutely. The skipper will anchor at protected spots like Cala del Faro or Cabopino, where the water is calm and clear. Snorkelling gear is usually available on request. What happens in bad weather? Your safety is the priority. If the forecast shows strong winds or high seas, we will offer you a free reschedule or full refund. The skipper monitors conditions and will adjust the route. How do we book a catamaran for our family? Contact us via WhatsApp on the number shown on our website. TITLE: Catamaran Rental Marbella 2026: Sail &amp; Power Catamarans from €350
DESCRIPTION: Looking for catamaran rental in Marbella? Our current fleet is two 12.5 m flybridge motor yachts from Puerto Banús (€749/2h). Plus a full guide to catamaran charter options in Marbella.

Home › Catamaran Rental Marbella 2026: Sail & Power Catamarans from €350 Our fleet right now: two 12.5 m flybridge motor yachts — the Astondoa 40 (9 guests) and Azimut 39 (11 guests). From €749 for 2h , up to €2,299 for a full 8-hour day . Skipper, fuel, drinks, insurance and VAT included. Catamaran rental in Marbella means a stable twin-hull platform, far more deck space than a monohull yacht of the same length, and a flat-water ride that keeps even seasickness-prone guests relaxed. Prices start at €350 for 4 hours on a 38-ft sail catamaran from Puerto Banús and scale up to €2,400 for a full day on a 50-ft luxury catamaran. Why a catamaran beats a monohull in Marbella Three concrete advantages for the typical Marbella day charter: Stability. The Costa del Sol gets a 12–18 knot easterly (the levante) most summer afternoons. A monohull yacht heels 15–20°; a catamaran heels 2–3°. Glasses stay on tables, kids stay calm, and lunch stays on the plate. Deck space. A 40 ft catamaran has the deck area of roughly a 55 ft monohull. Bridgedeck cockpit, two helm stations, forward trampolines for sun-lounging, and a swim platform across the full stern. Shallow draft. Catamarans typically draw 1.1–1.3 metres versus 2.0–2.5 metres for a monohull. The skipper can anchor closer to shore at Cala del Faro, Cabopino dunes or Río Real — which puts the swim ladder over clearer, calmer water. Catamaran rental Marbella prices 2026 Catamaran 4 h low 4 h high Full day 8 h Day guests 38–42 ft sail catamaran €350 €420 €1,000–€1,250 10–12 44–48 ft sail catamaran €450 €580 €1,400–€1,700 12 40–45 ft power catamaran €520 €680 €1,600–€1,900 10–12 50 ft luxury catamaran €700 €900 €1,800–€2,400 12–14 Prices include skipper, fuel and standard drinks. For comparison with motor yachts of similar length, see yacht charter Marbella . Sail vs power catamaran Sail catamarans are the romantic, atmospheric option. When the wind cooperates (most afternoons May–October), the skipper unfurls the genoa and you sail in near silence at 6–8 knots. The downside: under engine alone, sail catamarans only do 7–9 knots, so reaching Sotogrande and back in 4 hours isn't realistic. Power catamarans cruise at 18–22 knots with twin diesels, which makes long itineraries viable, but you trade the quiet sail experience for engine noise. For pure swim-and-lunch days where range doesn't matter, the sail catamaran is almost always the better experience. For Gibraltar trips or anywhere you want to cover ground, the power cat or a motor yacht makes more sense. Catamaran itineraries from Puerto Banús The 4-hour catamaran sweet spot from Puerto Banús: depart 11:00, motor west 30 minutes to clear the marina traffic, raise sails off Río Verde, sail the Golden Mile coastline downwind, drop sails and anchor at Río Real for a long swim, motor back to Puerto Banús by 15:00 in time for a beach club afternoon. For a full day, add a second anchor stop at Cala del Faro past Estepona — total round trip about 35 NM. If you have kids on board , the flat catamaran deck is dramatically safer than a heeling monohull. What's included Standard catamaran charter inclusions in Marbella are identical to motor yacht charters: skipper, fuel, soft drinks, water, ice, light snacks, snorkel gear and an inflatable SUP or donut. Many catamaran operators also throw in fishing rods (light tackle for tuna or mackerel) and the use of the on-board BBQ at anchor — ask when booking. Best months for catamaran rental in Marbella May, June, September and October are ideal — steady 8–14 knot wind for proper sailing, sea temperature 19–23 °C, and 10–15% lower prices than peak July/August. July and August deliver hotter weather but variable wind: sometimes glassy mornings (motor only) and stronger afternoons. November to March, sail catamaran trips still run on calm days but choice of operators is more limited. How to book Tell us your date, group size, sail vs power preference and budget. We'll send back specific catamaran options with photos and exact pricing. Confirm with 50% deposit; balance on the boarding day. The full boat rental Marbella hub compares catamarans against every other boat type if you're still deciding. Frequently asked questions Why pick a catamaran over a monohull yacht? Two reasons: stability and deck space. A catamaran sits flat on the water with two hulls — even in 15-knot wind there's almost no heel — so guests who get queasy on monohulls can usually relax. The bridgedeck and forward trampolines also give you 40–50% more usable deck space at the same overall length, which matters when you have 10+ guests. How much is catamaran rental in Marbella? Catamaran rental in Marbella starts at €350 for 4 hours on a 38-ft sail catamaran in low season, €420 in high season. An 8-hour day on the same catamaran is €1,000–€1,250 fully crewed. Larger 50-ft catamarans run €600 for 4 hours and €1,800–€2,400 for a day. Sail catamaran or power catamaran? Sail catamarans give you the option to actually sail when the wind is right (typically a Levante easterly mid-afternoon) — it's quieter and more romantic, but slower. Power catamarans (twin-engine, no rig) deliver 18–22 knot cruising, which matters if you want to reach Sotogrande or Cabopino on the same day. For lunch-and-swim half-days, sail catamarans win on atmosphere. How many guests fit on a catamaran? Day-charter capacity on the standard 38–42 ft catamarans in Marbella is 10–12 guests. Larger 50-ft catamarans take 14–16 day guests. Overnight capacity is lower — typically 6–8 in cabins. For groups above 16, look at boat party options on motor yachts. Are catamarans good for snorkelling? Excellent. The shallow draft (often 1.2 m vs 2.5 m for a monohull) lets the skipper anchor closer to shore, which usually means clearer water for snorkelling. The wide swim platforms at the stern make getting in and out far easier than climbing down a monohull ladder. ★★★★★ 4.9 · verified reviews From €749 2h skippered charter Instant quotes from local operators across Puerto Banús, Marbella Marina, Cabopino, Estepona & Sotogrande. 💬 Message on WhatsApp Avg reply < 5 min · No deposit until you confirm 📅 Book now Browse the full fleet → All charters include Licensed skipper & fuel Drinks: water, soft drinks, beer, white wine, cava Light snacks Insurance & safety equipment Snorkel gear & inflatables VAT 21% — no surprises

TITLE: Bootsführerschein in Spanien: Regeln 2026 für Marbella einfach erklärt
DESCRIPTION: Bootsführerschein in Spanien — wann du keinen brauchst, welche deutschen Scheine gelten und wie führerscheinfreies Fahren in Marbella funktioniert (5 m / 15 PS).

Bootsverleih › Bootsführerschein Spanien Die häufigste Frage deutscher Gäste: „Brauche ich für ein Boot in Marbella einen Führerschein?“ Die kurze Antwort: oft nicht. Hier sind die Regeln für 2026 klar erklärt. Wann du KEINEN Führerschein brauchst Mit Skipper — bei ~95% unserer Charters fährt ein lizenzierter Skipper. Du brauchst gar nichts und kannst dich entspannen. Führerscheinfrei selbst fahren — erlaubt bei Booten bis 5 m Rumpflänge und max. 15 PS , innerhalb 2 Seemeilen von der Küste, nur bei Tageslicht, Fahrer mindestens 18 Jahre. Siehe unsere Boote ohne Führerschein ab €230/2h. Welche deutschen Scheine in Spanien gelten Wer ein größeres Boot selbst steuern will, braucht eine anerkannte Lizenz. In der Praxis werden gängige internationale Scheine akzeptiert: SBF-See (Sportbootführerschein See) — für küstennahe Fahrten meist ausreichend. SKS (Sportküstenschifferschein) — für größere/weitere Charter. ICC (International Certificate of Competence) — international anerkannt. Bring immer das Original-Zertifikat (kein Foto) mit. Im Zweifel schick uns vorab ein Bild auf WhatsApp — wir sagen dir, ob es für das gewünschte Boot reicht. Die führerscheinfreien Grenzen im Detail Regel Grenze Bootslänge max. 5 m Motorleistung max. 15 PS Abstand zur Küste max. 2 Seemeilen Tageszeit nur bei Tageslicht Mindestalter Fahrer 18 Jahre Unser Tipp Die meisten Gäste buchen einfach mit Skipper — kein Papierkram, kein Stress, und ihr lernt die besten Buchten von einem Local. Wer den Nervenkitzel selbst fahren will, nimmt ein führerscheinfreies Boot oder eine geführte Jetski-Tour . ★★★★★ 4.9 · verifizierte Bewertungen Ab €749 2h Charter mit Skipper WhatsApp jetzt — durchschnittliche Antwort in unter 5 Minuten. Para cualquier cosa con grupo de 6+, comodidad, bebidas a bordo o llegar a sitios bonitos como Cala del Faro, nuestra opción con patrón sale a cuenta y es infinitamente más relajante. Sobre los patrones de nuestra flota Todos nuestros patrones tienen titulación oficial española (PER — Patrón de Embarcaciones de Recreo, o superior) y al menos 5 años de experiencia en la Costa del Sol. Conocen cada fondeo, cada chiringuito accesible por mar, las horas óptimas para evitar el viento de levante, y cómo maniobrar Puerto Banús un sábado de agosto. Hablan español, inglés y la mayoría también francés o italiano. Dejarán que conduzcas un rato en tramos seguros si te apetece probar el timón. Reglamentación española al detalle La normativa de embarcaciones sin titulación viene del Real Decreto 875/2014. Los límites simultáneos son: Eslora máxima: 5 m (motor) / 6 m (vela) Potencia máxima: 15 cv Distancia máxima de la costa: 2 millas náuticas (~3,7 km) Solo horario diurno, sin pernoctación Conductor con al menos 18 años cumplidos Misma normativa de alcohol que para conducción terrestre El Servicio Marítimo de la Guardia Civil hace patrullas aleatorias en julio-agosto, especialmente entre Puerto Banús y Cabopino. Si te paran y el motor supera los 15 cv en una embarcación supuestamente "sin titulación", la multa al alquilador es de €600+ y al conductor le retiran el timón en el momento. Por eso los operadores serios son estrictos con el límite. Preguntas frecuentes ¿De verdad puedo alquilar un barco sin licencia en Marbella? Sí — con dos opciones. Reserva un yate con patrón profesional (nuestra flota, desde €749/2h) y eres pasajero, sin ningún requisito de licencia. O alquila una embarcación pequeña (hasta 5 m / 15 cv) en operadores especializados, sin titulación pero con limitaciones (2 NM de costa, sólo de día). ¿Hace falta saber navegar? No con nuestros barcos — el patrón conduce. Sólo te sientas, disfrutas y das instrucciones del tipo "un baño más antes de volver". ¿Cuántos puedo llevar? Astondoa 40 hasta 9 invitados, Azimut 39 hasta 11, Mangusta 80 hasta 12. ¿Puedo conducir un rato? Sí, durante tramos seguros y bajo supervisión del patrón. Es una práctica habitual y los patrones suelen estar encantados de que pruebes el timón. Con nuestros clientes a bordo Charters reales con grupos reales en Marbella, Puerto Banús y la Costa del Sol. TITLE: Política de Privacidad — Alquiler de Barcos Marbella
DESCRIPTION: Política de privacidad de boatrentalinmarbella.com — qué datos recopilamos cuando nos contactas por WhatsApp, email o formulario, cómo los usamos y tus derechos RGPD.

Política de Privacidad Última actualización: 1 de junio de 2026 Esta política explica cómo Boat Rental Marbella (sitio web boatrentalinmarbella.com , en adelante "nosotros") recopila, utiliza y protege tus datos personales cuando visitas el Sitio, nos contactas por WhatsApp, email o el formulario de reserva, o contratas un chárter. Cumplimos con el Reglamento (UE) 2016/679 (RGPD) y la LOPDGDD 3/2018. 1. Responsable del tratamiento Boat Rental Marbella Marbella, Andalucía, España (29602) WhatsApp / teléfono: +358 400 406 194 2. Datos que recopilamos Reservas y consultas — nombre, teléfono, email, fechas de interés, número de personas, puerto de salida, idioma, y el texto libre que envíes. Pagos — para reservas confirmadas el pago lo procesa el operador del barco (normalmente Stripe, Revolut Business o transferencia). No guardamos números de tarjeta completos. Datos técnicos — dirección IP, navegador, dispositivo, página de origen, páginas vistas y marcas de tiempo. Recogidos por los logs del servidor y Google Analytics 4 (ID G-SPMRYJVTHD). Cookies — ver apartado 7. 3. Para qué los usamos (base jurídica) Atender tu consulta y organizar el chárter — base: ejecución de un contrato o medidas pre-contractuales (art. 6.1.b RGPD). Compartir la reserva con el operador / patrón — base: contrato (art. 6.1.b). Cumplir con la normativa fiscal y marítima española (facturación, lista de pasajeros si el capitán la requiere) — base: obligación legal (art. 6.1.c). Mejorar el Sitio y medir tráfico — base: interés legítimo (art. 6.1.f). Comunicaciones comerciales — solo con tu consentimiento expreso (art. 6.1.a), revocable en cualquier momento. Actualmente no enviamos newsletter. 4. Destinatarios Operador / patrón asignado al chárter (nombre, teléfono, fecha, número de personas). Procesadores de pago (Stripe, Revolut, etc.). Proveedores de comunicación — WhatsApp (Meta Platforms Ireland Ltd.), Gmail / Google Workspace, Instagram y Facebook (Meta). Alojamiento y analítica — GitHub Pages (Microsoft Corp., EE. UU.), Cloudflare, Google Analytics 4 (Google Ireland Ltd.). Hacienda, aseguradoras y autoridades cuando exista obligación legal. Algunos proveedores están en EE. UU. Las transferencias se basan en el Marco de Privacidad de Datos UE–EE. UU. o en las Cláusulas Contractuales Tipo de la Comisión Europea. 5. Conservación Consultas sin reserva — eliminadas en 12 meses. Reservas y facturas — 6 años (obligación fiscal española). Logs y analítica — 14 meses (por defecto en Google Analytics). Registros de consentimiento — hasta su retirada más un periodo razonable de archivo. 6. Tus derechos Puedes ejercer en cualquier momento los derechos de acceso, rectificación, supresión, limitación, oposición, portabilidad y retirada del consentimiento, enviándonos un WhatsApp al +358 400 406 194 con copia de un documento de identidad. Responderemos en un máximo de 30 días. También puedes reclamar ante la Agencia Española de Protección de Datos (AEPD) . 7. Cookies Estrictamente necesarias — para mostrar el Sitio, recordar el idioma y el borrador del formulario. No requieren consentimiento. Analítica — Google Analytics 4 ( _ga , _ga_* ) de forma anónima. Puedes desactivarlas con el complemento de inhabilitación de Google Analytics . Embeds externos — solo activan cookies si haces clic en enlaces a Instagram, Facebook o WhatsApp. 8. Menores El Sitio no se dirige a menores de 14 años y no recopilamos conscientemente sus datos. Los menores pueden viajar a bordo del chárter — sus datos los facilita el padre, madre o tutor legal en la reserva. 9. Seguridad El Sitio funciona sobre HTTPS. Los mensajes por WhatsApp están cifrados de extremo a extremo por Meta. Los registros internos se guardan en servicios cloud (Google Workspace) con acceso controlado y verificación en dos pasos. 10. Cambios Podemos actualizar esta política cuando sea necesario; la fecha de "Última actualización" arriba indica la versión vigente. Los cambios sustanciales se anunciarán en la portada durante al menos 30 días. 11. Contacto Cualquier consulta de privacidad: WhatsApp +358 400 406 194 . Consulta también nuestros Términos y Condiciones .

TITLE: Términos y Condiciones — Alquiler de Barcos Marbella
DESCRIPTION: Términos y condiciones de los alquileres de barcos reservados a través de boatrentalinmarbella.com — reserva, precios, pago, cancelación, meteorología, seguridad, responsabilidad y ley aplicable.

Términos y Condiciones Última actualización: 1 de junio de 2026 Estos términos regulan cualquier reserva, chárter, consulta o uso del sitio boatrentalinmarbella.com ("el Sitio"), operado por Boat Rental Marbella ("nosotros"). Al enviar una consulta, aceptar un presupuesto, abonar una señal o embarcar en un barco contratado, confirmas que has leído, entendido y aceptado estos términos. 1. Sobre nosotros Boat Rental Marbella es una agencia independiente de chárter con base en Marbella, Andalucía, España. Coordinamos chárteres con patrón de yates, catamaranes, lanchas y motos de agua que operan desde Puerto Banús, Puerto Deportivo de Marbella (Virgen del Carmen), Cabopino, Estepona y Sotogrande. Los chárteres son operados por patrones con licencia española y empresas colaboradoras con los permisos marítimos y comerciales correspondientes. WhatsApp / teléfono: +358 400 406 194 2. Proceso de reserva Nos envías una consulta a través del formulario, WhatsApp, email o DM de Instagram/Facebook, indicando fecha, número de personas y barco o experiencia preferida. Respondemos con disponibilidad y presupuesto por escrito (normalmente en pocas horas, a menudo en minutos durante el horario europeo). La reserva queda confirmada solo cuando (a) enviamos confirmación por escrito y (b) se recibe la señal o el pago total acordados. Te enviamos la dirección de salida, contacto del patrón, hora de quedada y briefing por WhatsApp al menos 24 horas antes del chárter. 3. Precios, pago y qué incluye Los precios se indican en euros (€), incluyen el IVA español (actualmente 21%) y — salvo indicación expresa — incluyen patrón con licencia, combustible para la ruta costera estándar, refrescos y agua, equipo de snorkel, paddleboard, toallas y seguro estándar. Lo siguiente normalmente no está incluido salvo mención: catering, bebidas premium, combustible de juguetes acuáticos (p. ej. salida en moto de agua fuera del chárter), tasas de atraque en puertos de terceros, propinas y extras opcionales (DJ, fotógrafo, decoración). Las formas de pago varían según el operador — habitualmente una señal del 30–50% por tarjeta, enlace Stripe, Revolut o transferencia SEPA para confirmar, y el resto en efectivo o tarjeta el día del chárter. Los términos concretos figuran en el presupuesto escrito. 4. Política de cancelación, modificación y reembolso Salvo que tu confirmación indique algo distinto, las condiciones estándar son: 7 o más días antes de la salida — reembolso del 100% de lo abonado. Entre 3 y 6 días antes — reembolso del 50%. Menos de 48 horas antes — sin reembolso. No presentarse — sin reembolso. Los cambios de fecha son gratuitos si se solicitan con al menos 72 horas de antelación y dependen de disponibilidad. 5. Política meteorológica El patrón es la única autoridad para decidir si la salida puede realizarse con seguridad. Si la previsión de viento supera la fuerza 4–5 (~20+ nudos), el estado de la mar es inseguro, o la autoridad portuaria emite una advertencia, el patrón aplazará el chárter — habitualmente la tarde anterior o antes de las 08:00 del mismo día. En ese caso te ofrecemos: una nueva fecha sin coste adicional (sujeto a disponibilidad), o el reembolso íntegro de lo abonado. La lluvia ligera por sí sola no es motivo de cancelación en la Costa del Sol. Si cancelas por motivos meteorológicos cuando el patrón considera la salida segura, aplican las condiciones del apartado 4. 6. Seguridad, conducta y autoridad del patrón A bordo, el capitán tiene plena autoridad legal y operativa sobre el barco y los pasajeros conforme a la legislación marítima española. El capitán puede, a su entera discreción y sin reembolso: denegar el embarque a personas visiblemente ebrias, bajo efectos de drogas o con conducta agresiva; alterar la ruta, acortar el chárter o regresar a puerto por motivos de seguridad; obligar al uso de chaleco salvavidas; prohibir el baño, los saltos desde el barco o el uso de juguetes acuáticos cuando las condiciones no sean seguras. Todos los pasajeros deben seguir las instrucciones del capitán y el briefing de seguridad. Los menores de 12 años deben llevar chaleco siempre que el barco esté en navegación. Las mascotas solo se aceptan si se ha acordado previamente y deben llevar un chaleco específico para perros aportado por el propietario. 7. Conducta, daños y limpieza Las drogas de cualquier tipo están terminantemente prohibidas a bordo — el capitán está obligado por ley a regresar a puerto y avisar a la Guardia Civil. El cliente es responsable de cualquier daño al barco, equipamiento, juguetes acuáticos o bienes de terceros causados por él o sus invitados por negligencia o dolo, incluyendo cristalería rota, tapicería manchada, equipo de snorkel perdido o dañado y limpieza extraordinaria (p. ej. vómitos, derrames de comida que requieran limpieza profunda — entre 150 € y 500 €). 8. Retrasos y prolongaciones El chárter comienza a la hora acordada. Si llegas tarde, el chárter finaliza igualmente a la hora prevista, sin extensión ni reembolso. Prolongar el chárter el mismo día suele ser posible si el siguiente turno está libre — el tiempo adicional se cobra al 80–100% de la tarifa horaria y debe acordarse con el patrón antes de finalizar el turno reservado. 9. Seguro Todo barco contratado cuenta con el seguro de casco y responsabilidad civil obligatorio según la legislación española. No cubre objetos personales (móviles, cámaras, joyas, gafas de sol), condiciones médicas preexistentes ni pérdidas causadas por el incumplimiento de las normas de seguridad. Recomendamos contratar un seguro de viaje con cobertura de chárter, especialmente en reservas de alto valor o grupos numerosos. 10. Fotografía y contenido Ocasionalmente el patrón o un operador de dron pueden tomar fotos o vídeos cortos durante el chárter. Al embarcar consientes el uso no identificativo de este material en nuestra web y redes sociales (Instagram, Facebook, TikTok, YouTube). Si no quieres aparecer, comunícaselo al patrón antes de zarpar y te excluiremos. Puedes retirar el consentimiento sobre imágenes ya publicadas escribiéndonos por WhatsApp al +358 400 406 194 . 11. Responsabilidad En la máxima medida permitida por la ley española, nuestra responsabilidad por cualquier pérdida derivada de tu chárter se limita al importe total pagado por dicho chárter. No respondemos por daños indirectos o consecuenciales (vuelos perdidos, alojamiento, pérdida de disfrute) causados por cancelaciones meteorológicas, fuerza mayor (temporales, órdenes gubernamentales, huelgas, pandemias, cierres portuarios) o actos de terceros. Nada en estos términos excluye la responsabilidad por fallecimiento o lesiones personales causadas por negligencia, ni cualquier otra responsabilidad que no pueda excluirse según la normativa española de consumo. 12. Divulgación de afiliación Algunos enlaces del Sitio apuntan a operadores o plataformas de reserva de terceros. Cuando recomendamos un operador podemos recibir una comisión si reservas a través nuestro. Esto nunca afecta al precio que pagas y solo destacamos operadores que nosotros mismos contrataríamos. 13. Propiedad intelectual Todo el texto, fotos, vídeos y gráficos del Sitio son © Boat Rental Marbella o se usan bajo licencia. Puedes compartir páginas concretas en redes sociales y enlazar al Sitio libremente. No puedes republicar, raspar (scraping) ni usar el contenido para entrenar modelos de IA sin nuestro permiso escrito. Los nombres de marcas de barcos (Astondoa, Azimut, Mangusta, Ferretti, etc.) pertenecen a sus respectivos fabricantes y se utilizan solo a efectos descriptivos. 14. Ley aplicable y jurisdicción Estos términos se rigen por la legislación española. Cualquier conflicto con un consumidor se resolverá ante los tribunales del lugar de residencia del consumidor dentro de la UE, o ante los tribunales de Marbella (Málaga) para clientes fuera de la UE. Los consumidores también pueden usar la plataforma europea de resolución de litigios en línea en ec.europa.eu/consumers/od

TITLE: Fishing Boat Rental Marbella 2026: Deep-Sea &amp; Inshore Charters
DESCRIPTION: Fishing boat rental Marbella — our 12.5 m motor yachts (Astondoa 40, Azimut 39) can run light tackle and trolling from €749/2h. Plus full guide to deep-sea and inshore fishing in Marbella.

From €749 for 2h , up to €2,299 for a full 8-hour day . Skipper, fuel, drinks, insurance and VAT included. Fishing boat rental in Marbella covers two distinct experiences: a quiet 2-hour inshore trip pulling sea bream and mackerel from 20-metre reefs off the Golden Mile, or a 4–8 hour deep-sea expedition chasing dorado and tuna 8–15 nautical miles offshore over deeper seamounts. Prices start at €220 with skipper, mate, rods and bait included. Fishing on our motor yachts Our 12.5 m fleet ( Astondoa 40 , Azimut 39 ) can run light tackle inshore fishing and trolling on request — same pricing as any other charter, €749 for 2 h up to €2,299 for a full 8-hour day . For dedicated deep-sea sportfishing with heavy tackle, livewell and a mate, message us and we will source a specialist boat through partners. What you can catch off Marbella, by season Dorado (mahi-mahi) — June to October. Schooling fish, electric strikes on trolled feathers, 4–12 kg average. The headline summer target. Bluefin tuna — May to July. Heavy tackle, stand-up gear, fish ranging 50–150 kg. Strict ICCAT quota: most Marbella charters are catch-and-release for recreational anglers. Amberjack — year-round, peak winter. Jigging or live bait over deep reefs at 30–80 m. Strong fighters, 5–25 kg. Bonito and Atlantic bonito — September to November. Easy fast action, great for kids. Inshore: sea bream, sea bass, mackerel, barracuda — year-round, light tackle, ideal beginner targets. Inshore vs deep-sea — which to book? Inshore (2–4 hours): stay within 2 NM of the coast, fish reefs and wrecks at 15–40 m depth, calm water, lighter tackle, lower price. Best for families, kids, first-timers, anyone who gets queasy. Deep-sea (4–8 hours): run 8–15 NM offshore to seamounts and current edges, troll lures or drift live bait, target bigger species, longer travel time, more boat motion. Best for serious anglers and groups happy to commit a full day. If you're undecided, the half-day inshore is the safer first booking — you can always upgrade next trip. For everything we offer across the fleet, the boat rental Marbella hub compares fishing alongside yachts and catamarans. Departure ports Puerto Banús hosts the biggest deep-sea sportfishers (10–12 m Bertram-class). Cabopino is the cheapest pickup for inshore trips and the closest harbour to the productive eastern reefs around Río Real. La Bajadilla fishing port (next to Marbella Marina) keeps the working-fleet feel and is where local skippers with 30+ years on the water are based. Estepona works for west-bound offshore tuna trips when current is favourable. What's included on every fishing charter Licensed skipper plus a mate (deep-sea) or just skipper (small inshore) Rods, reels and complete terminal tackle (hooks, leaders, swivels) Live bait (sardines, mackerel, squid) appropriate to target species Ice box for your catch Soft drinks and water Filleting and bagging of keepers at the dock Fishing licence coverage under the boat's commercial permit Not included: lunch (BYO sandwich or order a catered lunch box), alcohol (most skippers ask you to wait until you're back at the dock), and trip insurance for offshore days. Sample full-day offshore itinerary 07:00 Boarding at Puerto Banús pontoon 4, fuel and bait loaded the night before. 07:30 Run 45 minutes south-east to the Marbella seamount. 08:15 Set the trolling spread — 4 rods, lures alternating between dorado feathers and tuna konas. 11:00 First drift over deeper reef for amberjack and possible swordfish bonus. 13:00 Lunch break, drift fishing continues with lighter gear. 14:30 Run east towards Calahonda seamount for the afternoon bite. 16:00 Reel in, run back to Puerto Banús, mate fillets your catch on the dock. Booking tips For deep-sea, book a forecast window — Marbella's east wind (levante) above 15 knots makes serious offshore work uncomfortable. The skipper will reschedule weather days at no cost. From May to October the headliner is dorado (mahi-mahi) — schooling fish, fast bites, great for first-time anglers. Bluefin tuna season is May–July; expect 50–150 kg fish on heavy tackle. Do I need a fishing licence? Yes — Andalucía requires a Licencia de Pesca Marítima de Recreo for sport fishing. Can I keep the fish? Yes, within the daily quota. Andalucía allows 5 kg per person per day for recreational sea fishing, plus one fish over the size limit. You will: Throttle and brake. Right thumb forward to go, release to coast. Sea-Doos have an iBR brake-and-reverse system that makes docking much easier than older jet skis. Kill switch lanyard. Clipped to your life jacket. If you fall off, the engine stops automatically. The 200 m rule. Stay outside the swim-buoy line along every Marbella beach. Penalties are stiff and the Guardia Civil del Mar patrol. Wake awareness. Slow inside the Puerto Banús harbour mouth and when passing other boats — keep your wake low. After the briefing you take the Sea-Doo out for a controlled lap of the marina with our staff watching, and from there you're on your own. Multiple staterooms, chef-prepared meals, on-board tender. Day charter possible but most owners prefer multi-day. 30 m+ megayacht: charter market thins out fast. Usually weekly or longer, crew of 5-10, full-board. Our fleet — luxury-tier amenities at the 12.5 m size class We currently run two crewed 12.5 m flybridge motor yachts at €749 → €2,299 per charter — both with cream-leather interiors, AC saloon, two cabins, and the same skipper-fuel-drinks-insurance-VAT inclusion as larger luxury yachts. See Astondoa 40 and Azimut 39 for full specs. For 18 m+ proper superyachts (weekly charters, APA model, full crew with chef) we can source through partners — message us with dates and group size. Weekly charter and the APA model Multi-day and weekly charters on 24 m+ yachts use the global APA system. The base charter fee covers the yacht, captain and crew salaries. On top of that you pre-pay an Advance Provisioning Allowance (APA) of 25-30% which funds fuel, marina fees, food, drink and any extra crew expenses during the trip. Captain accounts for every euro and refunds the unused portion at the end. A 24 m yacht for a week in low season: ~€25,000 + ~€7,000 APA. Same yacht in August: ~€40,000 + €10,000 APA. The crew and what they actually do Captain: commands the yacht — navigation, anchoring, all decisions affecting safety. Holds at least a 200 GT commercial licence. Your single point of contact for the trip. Stewardess: guest service. Welcomes you on board, mixes drinks, plates the food, handles cabin turn-down on overnight charters, keeps the saloon and decks tidy. The stewardess role on a luxury yacht is the difference between "nice boat" and "luxury experience". Chef: from 24 m up. You fill in a preference sheet before the charter — favourite cuisines, dietary requirements, allergies — and the chef builds a tailored menu for the trip. Provisioning is done from local markets (Mercado de Puerto Banús, La Cañada). Deckhand / mate: handles lines, fenders, tender operation, water-toys deployment, and keeps the exterior immaculate. Often a deck cadet building sea time toward their captain qualification. Where you can go Day charters cover the Costa del Sol — Sotogrande in the west, Cabopino in the east, with the Golden Mile coast in between. A long day with an early start reaches Gibraltar by boat from Marbella (100 NM round trip, only viable on flat-sea days). Overnight luxury charters extend the cruising window along the Marbella coast and the Strait. Weekly bookings out of Marbella typically anchor the itinerary around Puerto Banús and the Golden Mile stops most guests want to see. The booking process WhatsApp inquiry — dates, group size, length (day/weekend/week), special requirements. Shortlist — we send 2-4 specific yachts with photos, plans, crew bios, day rates and any APA estimates. Hold — preferred yacht is held for 48 hours while you decide. Contract — MYBA Worldwide standard charter agreement, 50% deposit at signing. Preference sheet — sent 2-3 weeks ahead, captures food/drink/itinerary preferences. Boarding — exact pier number sent 24 hours ahead, balance paid on or before the day. For the full picture of what else is available across the fleet, see the boat rental Marbella hub. TITLE: Marbella vs Gibraltar Boat Rental: Which Is Better for Your Trip?
DESCRIPTION: Compare Marbella vs Gibraltar boat rental. We break down costs, distances, scenery, and amenities so you can choose the best Mediterranean charter for your group.

Home › Marbella vs Gibraltar Boat Rental: Which Is Better for Your Trip? When planning a Mediterranean boat trip, the choice between Marbella vs Gibraltar boat rental often comes down to value, scenery, and convenience. Both destinations offer Mediterranean waters, but the experience differs significantly. In this guide, we compare costs, cruising grounds, boat availability, and hidden extras so you can make an informed decision for your group. Cost comparison: Marbella vs Gibraltar boat rental Price transparency is where Marbella excels. Our all-inclusive rates start at €749 for two hours on an Astondoa 40 (12.5m, 9 guests) or Azimut 39 (12.5m, 11 guests). That price includes a licensed skipper, fuel, water, soft drinks, beer, white wine, cava, light snacks, insurance, and Spanish IVA (21%). For a full day (8 hours), the same boats cost €2,299 — no surprises. In Gibraltar, quoted rates often look cheaper at first glance — around €600-800 for a half-day on a 7-8m motorboat — but extras add up quickly. Fuel is rarely included and can cost €200-400 per trip. Gibraltar applies 20% VAT on top of the quoted price. Crew gratuity (10-15%) is also expected. A €600 half-day can easily become €900+. For larger groups, Marbella’s Mangusta 80 (24m, 12 guests) starts at €4,719 for a minimum 4 hours and includes a jet ski. Gibraltar’s equivalent-sized yachts are scarce and often priced on request, with no guarantee of inclusions. Cruising grounds and scenery Marbella’s coastline offers a mix of glamour and nature. Departing from Puerto Banús , you can cruise past the Golden Mile, anchor at Cala del Faro or Cala Cortés , or head west to Estepona (12 NM) or Sotogrande (25 NM). The backdrop of La Concha mountain and the Sierra Blanca provides stunning photo opportunities. Gibraltar’s main draw is the Rock of Gibraltar , but the coastline is more industrial, with container ports and tanker traffic. Anchoring spots are limited to the Bay of Gibraltar and Algeciras Bay. Dolphin-watching is popular, but the busy shipping lanes can detract from the experience. For swimming and relaxing in secluded coves, Marbella is the superior choice. Boat availability and fleet size Marbella’s fleet is extensive. We offer 17 boats ranging from a 6.4m Mariah SX21 (5 guests, €749/2h) to a 29m Ferretti 94 (12 guests, pricing on request). All depart from Puerto Banús. Whether you need a speedboat for a quick spin or a luxury flybridge for a full-day celebration, we have a vessel. Gibraltar’s charter fleet is smaller, typically RIBs and motorboats up to 10m. Larger luxury yachts are rare and often require advance booking. For group sizes above 8 guests, Marbella offers far more options. Inclusions and hidden costs Every Marbella charter includes: licensed skipper, fuel, water, soft drinks, beer, white wine, cava, light snacks, insurance, and 21% VAT. You pay the quoted price — nothing else. Gibraltar charters often exclude fuel, VAT, and sometimes even the skipper’s gratuity. Always ask for a full breakdown before booking. A typical Gibraltar charter might quote €700 but end up costing €950 after fuel (€200), VAT (€140), and gratuity (€70-100). Convenience for international visitors Marbella is served by Málaga Airport (AGP), 45 minutes away, with direct flights from most European capitals. Gibraltar’s airport (GIB) has limited routes and is often affected by cross-border delays. Marbella also offers a wider range of accommodation — from five-star hotels to budget apartments — and better dining and nightlife options. Which is better for your trip? Choose Marbella if you want transparent pricing, a larger fleet, beautiful coves, and a lively atmosphere. Choose Gibraltar only if you specifically want to see the Rock and are prepared for potential hidden costs. For most groups, Marbella offers a superior experience at a better overall price. Ready to book? Explore our full fleet and secure your Marbella charter today. Frequently asked questions Which destination offers better value for money: Marbella or Gibraltar? Marbella generally offers better value because our all-inclusive prices (skipper, fuel, drinks, snacks, VAT) start at €749 for two hours on an Astondoa 40. In Gibraltar, quoted rates often exclude fuel (€200-400 extra) and VAT (20%), so a €600 half-day can easily become €900+. Marbella’s pricing is transparent and includes everything. How far is the crossing from Marbella to Gibraltar by boat? The distance from Puerto Banús to Gibraltar Marina is approximately 35 nautical miles (about 1 hour 45 minutes at 20 knots). Most Marbella charters stay closer to the coast, visiting Estepona (12 NM) or Sotogrande (25 NM), which gives you more cruising time and less transit. Home › Marbella Yacht Charter Cancellation Policy: What You Should Know Booking a Marbella yacht charter cancellation policy is straightforward, but knowing the rules can save you money and stress. Deposit and Payment Terms To secure any yacht from our fleet—from the Marbella yacht charter lineup to specific models like the Azimut 58 Flybridge—a 50% deposit is required at booking. The remaining 50% is due 7 days before departure. For last-minute bookings (within 7 days), full payment is taken upfront. All payments include Spanish IVA (21%), and we accept bank transfers and major credit cards. Cancellation Windows and Refunds Our refund policy is tiered by how far in advance you cancel: 30+ days before charter: Full refund of all payments. 14–29 days before charter: 50% refund of total charter cost. Less than 14 days before charter: No refund. Cancellations must be submitted in writing via email or WhatsApp. Verbal requests are not accepted. Refunds are processed within 5–10 business days to the original payment method. Weather-Related Cancellations The safety of our guests and crew is paramount. If the licensed skipper determines that weather conditions pose a risk (e.g., winds exceeding 25 knots, heavy storms, or dangerous sea states), the charter will be cancelled with a full refund or the option to reschedule. We do not cancel for light rain or moderate chop—only for conditions that compromise safety. This policy applies to all boats, including the Ferretti 94 and smaller vessels like the Mariah SX21. Late Arrivals and No-Shows If you arrive late to Puerto Banús or fail to show up, no refund is given. The charter departs at the booked time and returns as scheduled, regardless of your arrival. We recommend arriving 15 minutes before departure to check in and meet the crew. This rule applies to all charters, from the Dubhe (8m, 5 pax) to the Mangusta 80 (Grey). Rescheduling and Date Changes You can change your charter date at no charge up to 14 days before departure, subject to availability. Within 14 days, date changes are treated as cancellations and follow the refund policy above. To reschedule, contact us via WhatsApp or email with your preferred new dates. We'll confirm availability and adjust the booking. Special Cases: Private Events and Corporate Charters For private events, corporate charters, or multi-boat bookings (e.g., a fleet of several Marbella yacht charter vessels), separate cancellation terms may apply. These are agreed in writing at the time of booking. Always review your contract for specific clauses regarding deposits, refunds, and force majeure. How to Cancel or Modify Your Booking To cancel or modify your charter, send an email to our bookings team or a WhatsApp message with your booking reference. We will confirm receipt and process the refund or change according to the policy. Keep a record of your cancellation request until the refund is received. For urgent changes, WhatsApp is fastest. The remaining balance is due 7 days before departure for standard bookings, or immediately for last-minute charters (within 7 days). Deposits are taken via bank transfer or card. Can I get a full refund if I cancel my yacht charter? Yes, if you cancel at least 30 days before the charter date, you receive a full refund of any payments made. Cancellations between 14 and 29 days receive a 50% refund. No refunds are given for cancellations less than 14 days before departure. What happens if bad weather forces cancellation? If the licensed skipper deems conditions unsafe (e.g., winds over 25 knots, heavy storms), you get a full refund or the option to reschedule at no extra cost. The charter departs at the booked time and returns as scheduled, regardless of your arrival time. We recommend arriving 15 minutes early at the marina. How do I cancel my booking? TITLE: Marbella Yacht Charter License Requirements: Do You Need One?
DESCRIPTION: Do you need a licence to charter a yacht in Marbella? Find out the Marbella yacht charter license requirements, plus boat specs, prices, and inclusions.

Home › Marbella Yacht Charter License Requirements: Do You Need One? Planning a yacht charter in Marbella and wondering about the Marbella yacht charter license requirements ? You don't need one. All our charters include a fully licensed skipper who takes care of everything—navigation, mooring, safety, and even the drinks. You just show up, relax, and enjoy the Mediterranean. Here's everything you need to know about licences, age limits, and what's included. No Licence Needed for Our Charters Every boat in our fleet departs from Puerto Banús with a professional skipper. That means zero paperwork, no exams, and no prior experience. Whether you're on a Boat Rental Marbella Astondoa 40 or a Mangusta 80, the skipper handles the helm. You simply sit back and take in the views of La Concha, the Golden Mile, and the Costa del Sol coastline. What About Bareboat Charters? If you want to rent a boat without a skipper (bareboat), Spanish law requires a recreational licence called the PER (Patrón de Embarcaciones de Recreo). This allows you to operate vessels up to 15m in length. However, we don't offer bareboat hire—all our charters are skippered. So for our fleet, a licence is never needed. Age and ID Requirements You must be at least 18 to book a charter. All passengers need a valid ID or passport, which the skipper checks at departure. There's no upper age limit, but everyone should be comfortable boarding and moving around the boat. Life jackets are provided for all sizes, including children. If you want to rent a boat without a skipper (bareboat), you'll need a Spanish recreational licence (PER) or an equivalent international certificate. What is the PER licence and do I need it? The Patrón de Embarcaciones de Recreo (PER) is a Spanish qualification for operating recreational boats up to 15m in length. It requires theory and practical exams. For our charters, you don't need it—our skippers take care of everything. Only consider it if you plan to hire a bareboat in Spain. Can I drive the boat myself during a skippered charter? Yes, with the skipper's permission and supervision, you can take the helm in open water. The skipper remains responsible for safety and navigation. International licences (ICC, RYA, USCG) are not required for our skippered charters. However, for bareboat hire in Spain, you may need to exchange your licence for a Spanish one or obtain a temporary permit. Check with the local maritime authority. Cost comparison: Marbella vs Ibiza When comparing yacht charter Marbella vs Ibiza , the most obvious difference is price.
